Reinforcement learning (RL) is a promising paradigm of modern artificial intelligence. An agent in RL acts under a specific policy, interacts with an unknown environment, observes environment state changes, receives rewards, and improves the policy. RL has demonstrated great potential in various applications, including autonomous driving Chen etВ al. (2015), robotics Gu etВ al. (2017), power networks Kar etВ al. (2013), to name a few.

Among many algorithms that are central to RL is the temporal-difference (TD) learning approach.TD learning provides a unified framework to evaluate a policy in terms of the long-term discounted accumulative reward. Within the family of TD algorithms, TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) is a popular one Sutton (1988). However, the classical TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) is a tabular-based approach, which stores the entry-wise value function state-by-state. In many RL applications, the number of elements in the state space is large. Thus, it is impractical or even impossible to evaluate the value function on a per state basis.This is also referred to as the curse of dimensionality. Therefore, TD with function approximation is usually preferable, which includes linear or non-linear approximators Mnih etВ al. (2015); Silver etВ al. (2016).

Going beyond the single-agent RL setting, many practical applications contain rewards distributed over multiple agents without a central coordinator. In this multi-agent RL (MARL) scenario, agents cooperate with each other to explore an unknown environment and accomplish a specific task Zhang etВ al. (2018); Wai etВ al. (2018); Chen etВ al. (2018); Lee etВ al. (2020); Zhang etВ al. (2019). A broad range of applications over mobile sensor networks Cortes etВ al. (2004) and power networks Kar etВ al. (2013) can be modeled as MARL problems. Typically, agents in MARL are assumed to be reliable; that is, they share accurate information with others. In this circumstance, TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) can be implemented over a MARL environment in a decentralized manner Doan etВ al. (2019).

However, the agents in MARL are not always reliable. Communication errors, data corruptions or even malicious attacks may happen during the training process. We model all these unreliable behaviors as Byzantine attacks Lamport etВ al. (1982); Yang etВ al. (2019). In this Byzantine attack model, adversarial agents are able to arbitrarily manipulate their outputs, collude with each other and inject false information into the MARL environment. Decentralized TD, and policy evaluation in general, in the presence of Byzantine agents are yet less understood areas.

To perform decentralized policy evaluation under Byzantine attacks, we propose a novel trimmed mean-based Byzantine-resilient decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with linear function approximation algorithm that we term Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). Different from existing decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) such as that in Doan etВ al. (2019), Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) is a robust version of TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). It uses a robust aggregation technique to alleviate the negative effect of Byzantine agents, and guarantees global convergence even under Byzantine attacks. However, the theoretical analysis, especially the non-asymptotic analysis of Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), is nontrivial. First, the existence of Byzantine agents prevents the honest agents from obtaining accurate information from their neighbors, and the induced error propagates through the TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) dynamics. Second, the fact that the TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) update does not follow stochastic gradient of any objective function brings a series of difficulties to the non-asymptotic analysis of Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) by leveraging the first-order optimization toolbox.

TD learning plays an important role in policy evaluation for RL. The family of TD methods include gradient TD Sutton etВ al. (2008, 2009), least-squares TD Lazaric etВ al. (2012); Bradtke and Barto (1996), least-squares policy evaluation NediДҮ and Bertsekas (2003). As a representative algorithm, TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) provides a unified framework for policy evaluation Sutton (1988), with the parameter О»вҲҲ[0,1]рқңҶ01\lambda\in[0,1] controlling the trade-off between approximation accuracy and convergence rate. Several existing works have shown the convergence of TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with linear function approximation.The works of Tsitsiklis and VanВ Roy (1997); Dayan (1992) focus on the asymptotic convergence and other steady-state properties of TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). Several works provide finite-time analysis Bhandari etВ al. (2018); Lakshminarayanan and Szepesvari (2018); Dalal etВ al. (2018); Sun etВ al. (2020b), but their results hold only when using projection operation or assuming independent and identically distributed (i.i.d.) noise. Some of these assumptions have been relaxed in the recent works of Srikant and Ying (2019). Building upon these works, convergence analysis of decentralized TD has been studied recently in Doan etВ al. (2019); Sun etВ al. (2020a); Cassano etВ al. (2020).

Some exploratory efforts have been made to robustify RL approaches. In the single-agent setting, algorithms have been developed to alleviate the negative effect from approximation error Lu etВ al. (2019), or to robustify the learned policy in making decisions Tirinzoni etВ al. (2018); Petrik and Russel (2019). However, little is known on how to robustify RL methods during the training stage in the single-agent RL setting, and in the MARL setting вҖ“ an even less explored area.

On the other spectrum, designing Byzantine-resilient algorithms has become a popular topic in distributed and decentralized machine learning, with applications mainly in supervised learning. Most algorithms in this regime replace the mean or weighted mean aggregation rules in Byzantine-free stochastic gradient methods with robust aggregation rules, such as geometric median Chen etВ al. (2017); Xie etВ al. (2018a), coordinate-wise median Yin etВ al. (2018), trimmed mean Xie etВ al. (2018b), Krum Blanchard etВ al. (2017), Bulyan ElВ Mhamdi etВ al. (2018), and RSA Li etВ al. (2019), or robustify the updates with malicious agent identification Alistarh etВ al. (2018). These aforementioned methods require a central node to coordinate the agents, which is different to our decentralized MARL setting. Existing decentralized Byzantine-resilient algorithms include the subgradient method with total variation-norm penalization Ben-Ameur etВ al. (2016); Peng and Ling (2020), BRIDGE Yang and Bajwa (2019), and MOZI Guo etВ al. (2020). However, these algorithms are all targeted to supervised learning either in i.i.d. or deterministic settings.Policy evaluation in MARL with adversarial agents is, by its nature, a stochastic optimization problem with non-i.i.d. and decentralized data. To the best of our knowledge, no Byzantine-resilient SGD-based algorithm has been developed in this regime.Therefore, existing Byzantine-resilient algorithms can not be applicable to policy evaluation, especially in MARL.

In the Byzantine-resilient decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) algorithm, each agent uses trimmed mean to aggregate neighboring messages. This strategy naturally generates a directed and time-varying graph that is a subset of the underlying communication network. Existing works have investigated decentralized optimization when the underlying communication network is directed and time-varying Yuan and Ho (2014); NediДҮ etВ al. (2017); NediДҮ and Olshevsky (2014). However, to the best of our knowledge, our work is the first to analyze decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) over a directed and time-varying graph.

The contributions of this paper are summarized as follows.

1. Targeting the robust policy evaluation in MARL, we propose a Byzantine-resilient decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with linear function approximation, abbreviated as Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), over decentralized and directed networks. Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) generalizes the robust aggregation rule Yang and Bajwa (2019); Vaidya (2012) to the regime of stochastic optimization, which is of independent interest.

2. To analyze our algorithm, we generalize the existing trimmed mean analysis to the stochastic setting with time-varying graphs. We establish the non-asymptotic analysis for Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) under Markovian observations.Our analysis implies that the network topology influences the convergence rate, and the asymptotic error is determined by the variation of local rewards and the degree of network unsaturation.

3. We conduct experiments using a standard MARL benchmark, the cooperative navigation task, over various networks. It is confirmed that Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) can successfully learn the linear value function estimate under Byzantine attacks.

In this section, we review some background on the policy evaluation, and then introduce our algorithm.

Consider an MARL environment consisting of N=|рқ’©|рқ‘Ғрқ’©N=|\mathcal{N}| honest agents and B=|в„¬|рқҗөв„¬B=|\mathcal{B}| Byzantine agents, where рқ’©рқ’©\mathcal{N} and в„¬в„¬\mathcal{B} denote the sets of honest agents and Byzantine agents, respectively. We illustrate MARL with Byzantine agents in Figure 1. In this environment, our goal is to evaluate a fixed policy in a Markov reward process (MRP).

TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with function approximation. One way to find the value function is to solve the so-termed Bellman equation, which is a system of linear equations of рқ’ұвҖӢ(s)рқ’ұрқ‘ \mathcal{V}(s), given byрқ’ұвҖӢ(s)=1NвҖӢвҲ‘sвҖІвҲҲрқ’®рқ’«вҖӢ(s,sвҖІ)вҖӢ(вҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©в„ӣnвҖӢ(s,sвҖІ)+ОівҖӢрқ’ұвҖӢ(sвҖІ)),вҲҖsвҲҲрқ’®.formulae-sequenceрқ’ұрқ‘ 1рқ‘Ғsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІрқ’®рқ’«рқ‘ superscriptрқ‘ вҖІsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©subscriptв„ӣрқ‘ӣрқ‘ superscriptрқ‘ вҖІрқӣҫрқ’ұsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІfor-allрқ‘ рқ’®\mathcal{V}(s)=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{s^{\prime}\in\mathcal{S}}\mathcal{P}(s,s^{\prime})\Big{(}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\mathcal{R}_{n}(s,s^{\prime})+\gamma\mathcal{V}(s^{\prime})\Big{)},~{}\forall s\in{\cal S}.(2)If рқ’«вҖӢ(s,sвҖІ)рқ’«рқ‘ superscriptрқ‘ вҖІ\mathcal{P}(s,s^{\prime}) is known and the number of elements in the state space |рқ’®|рқ’®|\mathcal{S}| is small, one can find рқ’ұвҖӢ(s)рқ’ұрқ‘ \mathcal{V}(s) by solving this system of linear equations. On the other hand, if рқ’«вҖӢ(s,sвҖІ)рқ’«рқ‘ superscriptрқ‘ вҖІ\mathcal{P}(s,s^{\prime}) is unknown yet |рқ’®|рқ’®|\mathcal{S}| is manageable, tabular-based TD methods have impressive performance.Unfortunately, when the number of elements in рқ’®рқ’®\mathcal{S} is large or even infinite, it is impractical to find an exact solution or even evaluate a solution to (2). Instead, one has to resort to function approximation of рқ’ұвҖӢ(s)рқ’ұрқ‘ \mathcal{V}(s).

To implement TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) in the MARL setting, every honest agent nрқ‘ӣn maintains its local copy рқңҪnkвҲҲв„қDsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptв„қрқҗ·\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}\in\mathbb{R}^{D}. At step kрқ‘ҳk, the honest agent nрқ‘ӣn observes the transition from state sksuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳs^{k} to sk+1superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1s^{k+1}, calculates the local reward rnksuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳr_{n}^{k}, updates the eligibility trace byрқ’ӣk=ОівҖӢО»вҖӢрқ’ӣkвҲ’1+П•вҖӢ(sk),superscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳрқӣҫрқңҶsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳ1bold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ\bm{z}^{k}=\gamma\lambda\bm{z}^{k-1}+\bm{\phi}(s^{k}),(7)and computes the local TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) increment at agent nрқ‘ӣn byрқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪnk):=(rnk+(ОівҖӢП•вҖӢ(sk+1)вҲ’П•вҖӢ(sk))вҠӨвҖӢрқңҪnk)вҖӢрқ’ӣk.assignsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқӣҫbold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1bold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳtopsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳ\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}):=\left(r_{n}^{k}+(\gamma\bm{\phi}(s^{k+1})-\bm{\phi}(s^{k}))^{\top}\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}\right)\bm{z}^{k}.(8)After computing their local increments, the agents communicate with each other to exchange the latest local parameters. The honest agent nрқ‘ӣn collects рқңҪmksuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳ\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k} from all in-neighbors mрқ‘ҡm in рқ’©nвҲӘв„¬nsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣsubscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣ\mathcal{N}_{n}\cup\mathcal{B}_{n}, averages them, and uses the local increment О·kвҖӢрқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪnk)superscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}) to update the local parameter asрқңҪnk+1=1Nn+Bn+1вҖӢвҲ‘mвҲҲрқ’©nвҲӘв„¬nвҲӘ{n}рқңҪmk+О·kвҖӢрқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪnk).superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ11subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ1subscriptрқ‘ҡsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣsubscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k+1}=\frac{1}{N_{n}+B_{n}+1}\sum_{m\in\mathcal{N}_{n}\cup\mathcal{B}_{n}\cup\{n\}}\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}+\eta^{k}\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}).(9)

The update rule (9) seems plausible. However, the main challenge of implementing (9) is that while рқңҪmksuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳ\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k} are true parameters for mвҲҲрқ’©nрқ‘ҡsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣm\in\mathcal{N}_{n}, they can be arbitrary vectors for mвҲҲв„¬nрқ‘ҡsubscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣm\in\mathcal{B}_{n}. But the honest agent nрқ‘ӣn cannot distinguish Byzantine agents from all the in-neighbors. Motivated by the Byzantine-resilient supervised learning algorithms Blanchard etВ al. (2017); Yang and Bajwa (2019); Guo etВ al. (2020), we will robustify (9) by incorporating coordinate-wise trimmed mean to resist Byzantine attacks. Before taking averages over the messages received from their in-neighbors, the agents first discard the outliers on a per coordinate basis. To be specific, the honest agent nрқ‘ӣn estimates the number of Byzantine neighbors Bnsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣB_{n} and chooses a trimming number qnвүҘBnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣq_{n}\geq B_{n}. At every dimension dрқ‘‘d, the honest agent nрқ‘ӣn discards the largest qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} and smallest qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} elements of the received messages before taking average. We use рқ’©nk+вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k+}(d) and рқ’©nkвҲ’вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k-}(d) to denote the index sets of discarded elementsрқ’©nkвҲ’вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k-}(d):=argвҒЎminв„і:{в„івҠӮрқ’©nвҲӘв„¬n,|в„і|=qn}вҖӢвҲ‘mвҲҲв„і[рқңҪmk]d,assignabsent:в„іformulae-sequenceв„іsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣsubscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣв„іsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ҡв„іsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle:=\underset{\mathcal{M}:\{\mathcal{M}\subset\mathcal{N}_{n}\cup\mathcal{B}_{n},|\mathcal{M}|=q_{n}\}}{\arg\min}\sum_{m\in\mathcal{M}}[\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}]_{d},(10a)рқ’©nk+вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k+}(d):=argвҒЎmaxв„і:{в„івҠӮрқ’©nвҲӘв„¬n,|в„і|=qn}вҖӢвҲ‘mвҲҲв„і[рқңҪmk]d,assignabsent:в„іformulae-sequenceв„іsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣsubscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣв„іsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘ҡв„іsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle:=\underset{\mathcal{M}:\{\mathcal{M}\subset\mathcal{N}_{n}\cup\mathcal{B}_{n},|\mathcal{M}|=q_{n}\}}{\arg\max}\sum_{m\in\mathcal{M}}[\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}]_{d},(10b)where [рқңҪmk]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}]_{d} represents the dрқ‘‘d-th element of рқңҪmksuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳ\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}. If we define рқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d):=рқ’©nвҲ’рқ’©nk+вҲ’рқ’©nkвҲ’assignsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳ\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d):=\mathcal{N}_{n}-\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k+}-\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k-} as the set of the remaining indexes, the Byzantine-resilient update of dimension dрқ‘‘d corresponding to (9) is[рқңҪnk+1]d=1Nn+BnвҲ’2вҖӢqn+1вҖӢвҲ‘mвҲҲрқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҲӘ{n}[рқңҪmk]d+О·kвҖӢ[рқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪnk)]d.subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘‘1subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ1subscriptрқ‘ҡsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҡрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘superscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k+1}]_{d}=\frac{1}{N_{n}+{B_{n}}-2q_{n}+1}\!\!\sum_{m\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d)\cup\{n\}}\!\![\bm{\theta}_{m}^{k}]_{d}+\eta^{k}[\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k})]_{d}.(11)The proposed Byzantine-resilient decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with linear function approximation is summarized in Algorithm 1.

We will discuss why trimmed mean is able to robustify the policy evaluation process. Intuitively, if the models sent by Byzantine agents are outliers, they will be discarded directly, so the output of trimmed mean will not go far away from the mean of true model. However, since trimmed mean aggregation discard 2вҖӢqn2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ2q_{n} models at each coordinate and qnвүҘBnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣq_{n}\geq B_{n}, at least qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} models from honest agents are discarded at the same time.Fortunately, trimmed mean can still approximate the true mean because information in the discarded models can be recover by that in рқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d).

Consider a simple scenario where a Byzantine agent nвҖІsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІn^{\prime} mixes into рқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d) and honest agents рқңҪnk+kвҲҲрқ’©nk+вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\bm{\theta}_{n^{k+}}^{k}\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k+}(d) and рқңҪnkвҲ’kвҲҲрқ’©nkвҲ’вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\bm{\theta}_{n^{k-}}^{k}\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k-}(d) are discarded. As a result, it satisfies that[рқңҪnk+k]dвүӨ[рқңҪnвҖІk]dвүӨ[рқңҪnkвҲ’k]d.subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k+}}^{k}]_{d}\leq[\bm{\theta}_{n^{\prime}}^{k}]_{d}\leq[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k-}}^{k}]_{d}.(12)As a result, [рқңҪnвҖІk]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n^{\prime}}^{k}]_{d} can be expressed as the linear combination of [рқңҪnk+k]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k+}}^{k}]_{d} and [рқңҪnkвҲ’k]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k-}}^{k}]_{d}, that is (with a constant yвҲҲ[0,1]рқ‘Ұ01y\in[0,1])[рқңҪnвҖІk]d=yвҖӢ[рқңҪnk+k]d+(1вҲ’y)вҖӢ[рқңҪnkвҲ’k]d.subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘рқ‘Ұsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘1рқ‘Ұsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle[\bm{\theta}_{n^{\prime}}^{k}]_{d}=y[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k+}}^{k}]_{d}+(1-y)[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k-}}^{k}]_{d}.(13)This example shows that it is possible to recover the information in the discarded models from honest agents ([рқңҪnk+k]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k+}}^{k}]_{d} and [рқңҪnkвҲ’k]dsubscriptdelimited-[]superscriptsubscriptрқңҪsuperscriptрқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘[\bm{\theta}_{n^{k-}}^{k}]_{d}) and the trimmed mean can be viewed as a linear combination of the models from neighbors.

While the trimmed mean has been used in other Byzantine-resilient algorithms Blanchard etВ al. (2017); Yang and Bajwa (2019); Guo etВ al. (2020), most of them cannot give a finite-time upper bound of consensus and convergence rate. All of them require either the gradient of the objective function or its unbiased stochastic estimate. The most relevant works Yang and Bajwa (2019) and Vaidya (2012) are based on deterministic gradient descent. This makes our analysis of Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) nontrivial.

In this section, we first provide some important properties of TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), and then establish the convergence and consensus analysis for Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). We will show the proof sketch in Section 4, and leave the proofs to the appendices.

In the TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) recursion given by (6), a stationary point of {рқңҪk}superscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ\{{\bm{\theta}}^{k}\} implies the increment to be рқҹҺ0\bm{0}. For the decentralized case, we characterize the stationary point first in terms of function value and then in terms of parameter. To do so, for any рқңҪвҲҲв„қDрқңҪsuperscriptв„қрқҗ·\bm{\theta}\in\mathbb{R}^{D}, define the global increment asрқ’ҲВҜkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқңҪ\displaystyle\bar{\bm{g}}^{k}(\bm{\theta}):=1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©рқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)assignabsent1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©superscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқңҪ\displaystyle:=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta})=1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©(rnk+(ОівҖӢП•вҖӢ(sk+1)вҲ’П•вҖӢ(sk))вҠӨвҖӢрқңҪ)вҖӢрқ’ӣkabsent1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©superscriptsubscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқӣҫbold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1bold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳtopрқңҪsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳ\displaystyle=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\left(r_{n}^{k}+(\gamma\bm{\phi}(s^{k+1})-\bm{\phi}(s^{k}))^{\top}\bm{\theta}\right)\bm{z}^{k}=рқҗҖkвҖӢрқңҪ+рқ’ғВҜk,absentsuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳрқңҪsuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳ\displaystyle=\mathbf{A}^{k}\bm{\theta}+\bar{\bm{b}}^{k},(14)where рқ’Ҳnksubscriptsuperscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ{\bm{g}}^{k}_{n} is given by (8), and the coefficients рқҗҖksuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳ\mathbf{A}^{k} and рқ’ғВҜksuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳ\bar{\bm{b}}^{k} are given byрқҗҖk:=рқ’ӣkвҖӢ(ОівҖӢП•вҖӢ(sk+1)вҲ’П•вҖӢ(sk))вҠӨвҖӢandвҖӢрқ’ғВҜk:=1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©rnkвҖӢрқ’ӣk.assignsuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқӣҫbold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1bold-italic-П•superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳtopandsuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳassign1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©superscriptsubscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳ\mathbf{A}^{k}:=\bm{z}^{k}\left(\gamma\bm{\phi}(s^{k+1})-\bm{\phi}(s^{k})\right)^{\top}\text{and}~{}~{}\bar{\bm{b}}^{k}:=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}r_{n}^{k}\bm{z}^{k}.(15)

Similarly, we define рқ’ғnk:=rnkвҖӢрқ’ӣkassignsubscriptsuperscriptрқ’ғрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ҹрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ’ӣрқ‘ҳ\bm{b}^{k}_{n}:=r^{k}_{n}\bm{z}^{k} satisfying 1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©рқ’ғnk=рқ’ғВҜnk1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©subscriptsuperscriptрқ’ғрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\bm{b}^{k}_{n}=\bar{\bm{b}}^{k}_{n}, so that the local update can be expressed as рқ’ҲnkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)=рқҗҖkвҖӢрқңҪ+рқ’ғnksuperscriptsubscriptрқ’Ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқңҪsuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳрқңҪsubscriptsuperscriptрқ’ғрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\bm{g}_{n}^{k}(\bm{\theta})=\mathbf{A}^{k}\bm{\theta}+\bm{b}^{k}_{n}.

Observe that рқҗҖksuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳ\mathbf{A}^{k} and рқ’ғВҜksuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳ\bar{\bm{b}}^{k} are both determined by the state trajectory {s0,s1,вӢҜ,sk}superscriptрқ‘ 0superscriptрқ‘ 1вӢҜsuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ\{s^{0},s^{1},\cdots,s^{k}\} generated from the Markov chain. Therefore, to characterize the stationarity of{рқ’ҲВҜkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)}superscriptВҜрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқңҪ\{\bar{\bm{g}}^{k}(\bm{\theta})\},we require the Markov chain to satisfy the following assumption.

As highlighted in Tsitsiklis and VanВ Roy (1997), Assumption 1 guarantees the existence of the stationary distribution ПҒрқңҢ\rho of state sksuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳs^{k} and the expectation limits of рқҗҖksuperscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳ\mathbf{A}^{k} and рқ’ғВҜksuperscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳ\bar{\bm{b}}^{k}, aslimkвҶ’вҲһрқ”јвҖӢ[рқҗҖk]=рқҗҖвҲ—andlimkвҶ’вҲһрқ”јвҖӢ[рқ’ғВҜk]=рқ’ғВҜвҲ—.formulae-sequencesubscriptвҶ’рқ‘ҳрқ”јdelimited-[]superscriptрқҗҖрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқҗҖandsubscriptвҶ’рқ‘ҳрқ”јdelimited-[]superscriptВҜрқ’ғрқ‘ҳsuperscriptВҜрқ’ғ\lim_{k\to\infty}\mathbb{E}[\mathbf{A}^{k}]=\mathbf{A}^{*}\quad\text{and}\quad\lim_{k\to\infty}\mathbb{E}[\bar{\bm{b}}^{k}]=\bar{\bm{b}}^{*}.(16)Therefore, the limit of the global increment can be defined aslimkвҶ’вҲһрқ”јвҖӢ[рқ’ҲВҜkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)]=рқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪ)вҖӢwithвҖӢрқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪ):=рқҗҖвҲ—вҖӢрқңҪ+рқ’ғВҜвҲ—.subscriptвҶ’рқ‘ҳрқ”јdelimited-[]superscriptВҜрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқңҪsuperscriptВҜрқ’ҲрқңҪwithsuperscriptВҜрқ’ҲрқңҪassignsuperscriptрқҗҖрқңҪsuperscriptВҜрқ’ғ\lim_{k\to\infty}\mathbb{E}[\bar{\bm{g}}^{k}(\bm{\theta})]=\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta})~{}~{}~{}{\rm with}~{}~{}~{}\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta}):=\mathbf{A}^{*}\bm{\theta}+\bar{\bm{b}}^{*}.(17)It has been shown that рқҗҖвҲ—superscriptрқҗҖ\mathbf{A}^{*} and рқ’ғВҜвҲ—superscriptВҜрқ’ғ\bar{\bm{b}}^{*} have explicit expressions and рқҗҖвҲ—superscriptрқҗҖ\mathbf{A}^{*} is a negative definite matrix Tsitsiklis and VanВ Roy (1997). In addition, рқҗҖвҲ—superscriptрқҗҖ\mathbf{A}^{*} and рқ’ғВҜвҲ—superscriptВҜрқ’ғ\bar{\bm{b}}^{*} will be attracted to their limits at a geometric mixing rate Doan etВ al. (2019); Bhandari etВ al. (2018). These properties are presented in the supplementary, as well as the full version of this paper Wu etВ al. (2020).

If there exists рқңҪО»вҲһвҲҲв„қDsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶsuperscriptв„қрқҗ·\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}\in\mathbb{R}^{D} such that рқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪО»вҲһ)=рқҹҺsuperscriptВҜрқ’ҲsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ0\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda})=\bm{0}, we say that рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda} is a stationary point. We will show that our proposed Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) converges to a neighborhood of рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda} due to Byzantine attacks. Note that although we can solve (3) with either gradient descent or TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), their stationary points are different. The stationary point of gradient descent minimizes FвҖӢ(рқңҪ)рқҗ№рқңҪF(\bm{\theta}), while in TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), different О»рқңҶ\lambda leads to different FвҖӢ(рқңҪО»вҲһ)рқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶF(\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}) because the function рқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’ҲрқңҪ\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta}) depends on О»рқңҶ\lambda. This is one of the major challenges in analyzing Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). It has been shown in Tsitsiklis and VanВ Roy (1997) that рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda} satisfiesminрқңҪвҒЎFвҖӢ(рқңҪ)вүӨFвҖӢ(рқңҪО»вҲһ)вүӨ1вҲ’ОівҖӢО»1вҲ’ОівҖӢminрқңҪвҒЎFвҖӢ(рқңҪ).subscriptрқңҪрқҗ№рқңҪрқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ1рқӣҫрқңҶ1рқӣҫsubscriptрқңҪрқҗ№рқңҪ\min_{\bm{\theta}}F(\bm{\theta})\leq F(\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda})\leq\frac{1-\gamma\lambda}{1-\gamma}\min_{\bm{\theta}}F(\bm{\theta}).(18)Larger О»рқңҶ\lambda usually leads to smaller approximation error of рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda} in the original TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). However, as we can see later, this does not necessarily holdwhen confronting with the Byzantine agents.

Denote the filtration containing all the information up to time kрқ‘ҳk by в„ұk={s0,s1,вӢҜ,sk}superscriptв„ұрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ 0superscriptрқ‘ 1вӢҜsuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ\mathcal{F}^{k}=\{s^{0},s^{1},\cdots,s^{k}\}. Unlike the analysis of stochastic optimization, the conditional expectation of рқ’ҲВҜkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқңҪ\bar{\bm{g}}^{k}(\bm{\theta}) is usually not equal to рқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’ҲрқңҪ\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta}) even when kрқ‘ҳk is large enough, because рқ’«вҖӢ(sk+1=s|в„ұk)рқ’«superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1conditionalрқ‘ superscriptв„ұрқ‘ҳ{\cal P}(s^{k+1}=s|\mathcal{F}^{k}) is not equal to the stationary probability ПҒвҖӢ(s)рқңҢрқ‘ \rho(s) even when kрқ‘ҳk goes to infinity. As a result, рқ’ҲВҜkвҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’Ҳрқ‘ҳрқңҪ\bar{\bm{g}}^{k}(\bm{\theta}) is a biased estimator of рқ’ҲВҜвҲ—вҖӢ(рқңҪ)superscriptВҜрқ’ҲрқңҪ\bar{\bm{g}}^{*}(\bm{\theta}).This brings another of the major challenges to establish the convergence of Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda). To overcome this issue, we will resort to the geometric mixing time of Markov chain BrГ©maud (2013).

Before presenting our main results, we first introduce several assumptions.

The quantity Оҙ2superscriptрқӣҝ2\delta^{2} in Assumption 2 is the measurement of agent heterogeneity. When all agents have access to the global reward, Оҙ2superscriptрқӣҝ2\delta^{2} is equal to 00. As we will demonstrate in the analysis, a large Оҙ2superscriptрқӣҝ2\delta^{2} increases the difficulty of defending against the Byzantine attacks.

Assumption 3 is standard in analyzing the TD-family algorithms Doan etВ al. (2019); Bhandari etВ al. (2018); Srikant and Ying (2019).

We need an additional assumption on the network topology. Consider a set в„Ӣрқ’ўsubscriptв„Ӣрқ’ў\mathcal{H}_{\mathcal{G}} with cardinality Hрқ’ў=|в„Ӣрқ’ў|subscriptрқҗ»рқ’ўsubscriptв„Ӣрқ’ўH_{\mathcal{G}}=|\mathcal{H}_{\mathcal{G}}| whose elements are the subgraphs of рқ’ўрқ’ў\mathcal{G} obtained by removing all Byzantine agents with their edges, and removing any additional qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} incoming edges at every honest node nрқ‘ӣn.

We call nвҲ—superscriptрқ‘ӣn^{*} and П„рқ’ўsubscriptрқңҸрқ’ў\tau_{\mathcal{G}} as source node and network diameter, respectively.Examples of topologies that satisfy Assumption 4 have been discussed in Vaidya etВ al. (2012).

With these assumptions, we establish our main results. We first show all parameters in {рқңҪnk}subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\{\bm{\theta}^{k}_{n}\} will reach consensus albeit the Byzantine agents are biasing the learning process.

Theorem 1 implies that all honest agents eventually reach consensus, at the rate of OвҖӢ((О·k)2)рқ‘ӮsuperscriptsuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ2O\left((\eta^{k})^{2}\right). A smaller network diameter П„рқ’ўsubscriptрқңҸрқ’ў\tau_{\mathcal{G}} yields a faster convergence rate, as indicated by (21).

Next, we show that рқңҪnksubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\bm{\theta}^{k}_{n} on every honest agent nрқ‘ӣn converges to a neighborhood of рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}, the stationary point of the TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) recursion without Byzantine attacks.

Theorem 2 asserts that рқңҪnksubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ\bm{\theta}^{k}_{n} on every honest agent nрқ‘ӣn converges to a neighborhood of рқңҪО»вҲһsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}, with the rate dominated by the function ПҶПөвҖӢ(k)subscriptрқң‘italic-Пөрқ‘ҳ\varphi_{\epsilon}(k). When Пө>1italic-Пө1\epsilon>1, the algorithm converges at the rate of OвҖӢ(lnвҒЎ(k)/k)рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳO(\ln(k)/k), which is consistent with the rate in Bhandari etВ al. (2018). When Пө=1italic-Пө1\epsilon=1, the algorithm converges at the rate of O(ln(k)2/k)O(\ln(k)^{2}/k), which is consistent with the rate in Doan etВ al. (2019). When 0<Пө<10italic-Пө10<\epsilon<1, the algorithm converges at the rate of OвҖӢ(1/kПө)рқ‘Ӯ1superscriptрқ‘ҳitalic-ПөO(1/k^{\epsilon}). The radius of the neighborhood is bounded by a constant OвҖӢ(Dрқ’ўвҖӢОҙ2)рқ‘Ӯsubscriptрқҗ·рқ’ўsuperscriptрқӣҝ2O(D_{\mathcal{G}}\delta^{2}). To the best of our knowledge, this tight analysis is new.

In addition to the learning error caused by Byzantine attacks as shown in (23), the following corollary gives the overall asymptotic learning error.

The first term at the right-hand side of (27) comes from the Byzantine attacks and the use of trimmed mean, while the second term is due to the intrinsic error of linear approximation. Tuning the parameter О»рқңҶ\lambda helps achieve the best accuracy.

In this section, we will give the key idea of proving the main results. As explained in Section 2.3, we can view the trimmed mean as a linear combination of models, which enables us to express the trimmed mean aggregation in a compact form.

To see so, we first introduce some notations. With the trimmed mean aggregation, at each iteration kрқ‘ҳk, every agent discards some messages that may come from different agents. As a result, the communication graph is essentially a directed and time-varying subgraph of рқ’ўрқ’ў\mathcal{G} (even рқ’ўрқ’ў\mathcal{G} is undirected).Therefore, we analyze Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) by analyzing a more general algorithm вҖ” decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) over a time-varying directed network, which by itself is new, and of independent interest.

Theorem 3 implies that all agents eventually reach consensus, at the rate of OвҖӢ((О·k)2)рқ‘ӮsuperscriptsuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ2O\left((\eta^{k})^{2}\right).

Theorems 3 and 4 are the cornerstones to prove Theorems 1 and 2, respectively. The remaining task is to show the effect of trimmed mean in Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) can be described by a well-defined matrix рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d) satisfying (c1)вҖ“(c6).

The main different between our construction and that in Vaidya (2012) is how to choose the weights in Case 2.

With the definition of рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d) in (37), we can write Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) update in the form of (29), where рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d) satisfies conditions (c1)вҖ“(c6).

We test the proposed Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) on the cooperative navigation task that modifies the one in (Lowe etВ al., 2017). The goal of every agent is to cover its target landmark. An agentвҖҷs local reward is computed by calculating the distance between itself and its target landmark and, is further penalized if it collides with other agents. In every step, an agent chooses an action among {uвҖӢp,lвҖӢeвҖӢfвҖӢt,rвҖӢiвҖӢgвҖӢhвҖӢt,dвҖӢoвҖӢwвҖӢn}рқ‘ўрқ‘қрқ‘ҷрқ‘’рқ‘“рқ‘Ўрқ‘ҹрқ‘–рқ‘”в„Һрқ‘Ўрқ‘‘рқ‘ңрқ‘Өрқ‘ӣ\{up,left,right,down\} according to its policy. The local reward of each agent depends on the distance between the agent and its goal landmark, and will be penalized if the agent collides with others. Each agent does not know othersвҖҷ landmarks, and thus the local reward functions are kept private. Unlike the task in (Lowe etВ al., 2017), where every agent does not have a specific target landmark but has access to all local rewards, our setting is fully decentralized. The policy to be evaluated is uniform random. The performance metrics are the mean squared Bellman error (MSBE) and the mean consensus error (MCE). At every step, every honest agent has a local squared Bellman error (SBE) defined asSBEвҖӢ({рқңҪnk}n=1рқ’©,sk):=1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©(VрқңҪnkвҖӢ(sk)вҲ’вҲ‘sвҖІвҲҲрқ’®рқ’«вҖӢ(sk,sвҖІ)вҖӢ(в„ӣnвҖӢ(sk,sвҖІ)+ОівҖӢVрқңҪnkвҖӢ(sвҖІ)))2,assignSBEsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ1рқ’©superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳ1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©superscriptsubscriptрқ‘үsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳsubscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІрқ’®рқ’«superscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІsubscriptв„ӣрқ‘ӣsuperscriptрқ‘ рқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІрқӣҫsubscriptрқ‘үsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳsuperscriptрқ‘ вҖІ2\displaystyle\texttt{SBE}\left(\{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}\}_{n=1}^{\mathcal{N}},s^{k}\right):=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\left(V_{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}}(s^{k})-\sum_{s^{\prime}\in\mathcal{S}}\mathcal{P}(s^{k},s^{\prime})\big{(}\mathcal{R}_{n}(s^{k},s^{\prime})+\gamma V_{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}}(s^{\prime})\big{)}\right)^{2},(38)and a local consensus error (CE) defined asCEвҖӢ({рқңҪnk}n=1рқ’©):=1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©вҖ–рқңҪnkвҲ’рқңҪВҜkвҖ–2.assignCEsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣ1рқ’©1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©superscriptnormsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣsuperscriptВҜрқңҪрқ‘ҳ2\displaystyle\texttt{CE}\left(\{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{k}\}_{n=1}^{\mathcal{N}}\right):=\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\|\bm{\theta}^{k}_{n}-\bar{\bm{\theta}}^{k}\|^{2}.(39)

MSBE and MCE are calculated by averaging the local SBEs and CEs over all honest agents and all previous steps, respectively, given byMSBE:=1kвҖӢвҲ‘Оә=1kSBEвҖӢ({рқңҪnОә}n=1рқ’©,sОә)andMCE:=1kвҖӢвҲ‘Оә=1kCEвҖӢ({рқңҪnОә}n=1рқ’©)formulae-sequenceassignMSBE1рқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқң…1рқ‘ҳSBEsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқң…рқ‘ӣ1рқ’©superscriptрқ‘ рқң…andassignMCE1рқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқң…1рқ‘ҳCEsuperscriptsubscriptsuperscriptsubscriptрқңҪрқ‘ӣрқң…рқ‘ӣ1рқ’©\displaystyle\texttt{MSBE}:=\frac{1}{k}\sum_{\kappa=1}^{k}\texttt{SBE}\left(\{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{\kappa}\}_{n=1}^{\mathcal{N}},s^{\kappa}\right)~{}~{}~{}~{}~{}~{}{\rm and}~{}~{}~{}~{}~{}~{}\texttt{MCE}:=\frac{1}{k}\sum_{\kappa=1}^{k}\texttt{CE}\left(\{\bm{\theta}_{n}^{\kappa}\}_{n=1}^{\mathcal{N}}\right)(40)

Byzantine-resilience. We compare four algorithms: mean and trim refer to that the honest agents update their parameters via mean and trimmed mean using their neighboring parameters without Byzantine attacks, respectively; mean-attack and trim-attack refer to those under Byzantine attacks. That is, mean and mean-attack correspond to the original decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda), while trim and trim-attack correspond to Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda).We consider sign flipping attacks here.We examine the impact of different О»рқңҶ\lambda. For О»=0,0.3,0.6рқңҶ00.30.6\lambda=0,0.3,0.6, the step size is О·k=0.1ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.1рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.1}{\sqrt{k}}. For О»=0.9рқңҶ0.9\lambda=0.9, the step size is О·k=0.05ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.05рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.05}{\sqrt{k}}. The first underlying network is complete, with 777 honest and 222 Byzantine agents, and qn=2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ2q_{n}=2. The second is an Erdos-Renyi network with 999 agents. Every pair of agents are neighbors with probability 0.70.70.7, and every agent is Byzantine with probability 0.20.20.2. We set qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} as the number of Byzantine agents. A total of 10 random Erdos-Renyi graphs are generated to calculate the averaged MSBE and MCE. The Byzantine agents are normal in mean and trim, but adopt sign flipping attacks in mean-attack and trim-attack. Here, sign flipping attacks mean that Byzantine agents send negative values of their true parameters to its neighbors.

As shown in Figures 2 and 3, when the Byzantine agents are absent, decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with mean and trimmed mean aggregation rules both work well. At presence of Byzantine attacks, decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with mean aggregation fails, but the proposed trimmed mean aggregation rule is still robust. With particular note, as predicted by Theorem 1, CE is in the order of OвҖӢ((О·k)2)=OвҖӢ(1k)рқ‘ӮsuperscriptsuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ2рқ‘Ӯ1рқ‘ҳO((\eta^{k})^{2})=O(\frac{1}{k}), such that MCE is in the order of OвҖӢ(1kвҖӢвҲ‘Оә=1k(О·Оә)2)=OвҖӢ(lnвҒЎ(k)/k)рқ‘Ӯ1рқ‘ҳsuperscriptsubscriptрқң…1рқ‘ҳsuperscriptsuperscriptрқңӮрқң…2рқ‘Ӯрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳO(\frac{1}{k}\sum_{\kappa=1}^{k}(\eta^{\kappa})^{2})=O(\ln(k)/k) and MCEГ—k/lnвҒЎ(k)absentрқ‘ҳрқ‘ҳ\times k/\ln(k) becomes a horizontal line asymptotically. Our numerical experiments corroborate this theoretical result.

Network topology. We test the algorithms over different topologies. We have presented the performance in complete and Erdos-Renyi graphs under sign flipping attacks in Figures 2 and 3.In Figures 5 and 6, we test the algorithm in several decentralized networks shown in Figure 4. In these experiments, qn=1subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ1q_{n}=1. For О»=0,0.3,0.6рқңҶ00.30.6\lambda=0,0.3,0.6, the step size is set as О·k=0.1ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.1рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.1}{\sqrt{k}}. For О»=0.9рқңҶ0.9\lambda=0.9, О·k=0.05ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.05рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.05}{\sqrt{k}}.Byzantine agents are normal in mean and trim, but adopt sign flipping attacks in mean-attack and trim-attack.

Different Byzantine attacks. The robustness of the algorithms has been tested under different attacks. In Figures 7 and 8, we test same value and Gaussian noise attacks in the Erdos-Renyi graph. With same value attacks, Byzantine agents always share zero vectors. In Gaussian noise attacks, each Byzantine agent shares a randomly picked honest agentвҖҷs parameter, polluted with Gaussian noise (with mean 00 and standard deviation 111). For О»=0,0.3,0.6рқңҶ00.30.6\lambda=0,0.3,0.6, the step size is set as О·k=0.1ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.1рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.1}{\sqrt{k}}. For О»=0.9рқңҶ0.9\lambda=0.9, О·k=0.05ksuperscriptрқңӮрқ‘ҳ0.05рқ‘ҳ\eta^{k}=\frac{0.05}{\sqrt{k}}. A total of 5 random Erdos-Renyi graphs are generated to calculate the averaged MSBE and MCE. In these experiments, qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} is set to be the number of Byzantine agents in the graph.

This paper deals with temporal-difference learning in the MARL problem and proposes a novel Byzantine-resilient decentralized TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda) with linear function approximation. We establish the finite-time convergence rate and asymptotic learning error in the presence of Byzantine attacks. We show that the asymptotic learning error is determined by the variation of local rewards and the degree of network unsaturation. Numerical experiments corroborate the robustness of the proposed algorithm. Future work includes adaptively estimating the upper bound on the number of Byzantine agents.

4вҖӢ(Nn+BnвҲ’2вҖӢqnвҲ’BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d))вҖӢ(qnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d))вүӨ(NnвҲ’qn)24subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘superscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ24(N_{n}+B_{n}-2q_{n}-B^{k*}_{n}(d))(q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d))\leq(N_{n}-q_{n})^{2}.

As a result, in total NnвҲ’qn+1subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ1N_{n}-q_{n}+1 elements have the lower bound Ој0subscriptрқңҮ0\mu_{0}: Nn+BnвҲ’2вҖӢqnвҲ’BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘N_{n}+B_{n}-2q_{n}-B^{k*}_{n}(d) elements in рқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҲ©рқ’©nsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣ\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d)\cap\mathcal{N}_{n}, qnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d) elements in в„’nk+вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptв„’рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{L}_{n}^{k+}(d) or в„’nkвҲ’вҖӢ(d)superscriptsubscriptв„’рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathcal{L}_{n}^{k-}(d), as well as the element nрқ‘ӣn.Therefore Condition (c4) holds with constantОј0:=minnвҲҲрқ’©assignsubscriptрқңҮ0subscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©\displaystyle\mu_{0}:=\min_{n\in\mathcal{N}}{Nn+BnвҲ’3вҖӢqnNnвҲ’2вҖӢqn,(Nn+BnвҲ’2вҖӢqn)вҖӢ(qnвҲ’Bn)(NnвҲ’qn)2}Г—1Nn+BnвҲ’2вҖӢqn+1.subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ3subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ21subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣ2subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ1\displaystyle\left\{\frac{N_{n}+B_{n}-3q_{n}}{N_{n}-2q_{n}},\frac{(N_{n}+B_{n}-2q_{n})(q_{n}-B_{n})}{(N_{n}-q_{n})^{2}}\right\}\times\frac{1}{N_{n}+B_{n}-2q_{n}+1}.(93)

Verification of (c5) for Case 2. In Case 2, for mвҲҲрқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҲ©рқ’©nрқ‘ҡsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣm\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d)\cap\mathcal{N}_{n}, we mвҲҲв„’nk+вҖӢ(d)вҖӢorвҖӢв„’nkвҲ’вҖӢ(d)рқ‘ҡsuperscriptsubscriptв„’рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘orsuperscriptsubscriptв„’рқ‘ӣlimit-fromрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘m\in\mathcal{L}_{n}^{k+}(d)~{}\text{or}~{}\mathcal{L}_{n}^{k-}(d), that[рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)]nвҖӢm=subscriptdelimited-[]superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҡabsent\displaystyle[\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d)]_{nm}=1qnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҖӢвҲ‘nвҖІвҲҲрқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҲ©рқ’©nyвҖӢ(nвҖІ,m)вҖӢ1NnвҲ—вҖӢcnkвҖӢ(d)1subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘Ұsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІрқ‘ҡ1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsuperscriptsubscriptрқ‘җрқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\displaystyle\frac{1}{q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d)}\sum_{n^{\prime}\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d)\cap\mathcal{N}_{n}}y(n^{\prime},m)\frac{1}{N^{*}_{n}}c_{n}^{k}(d)+1qnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҖӢвҲ‘nвҖІвҲҲрқ’©nkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҲ©в„¬nyвҖӢ(nвҖІ,m)вҖӢ1NnвҲ—1subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІsuperscriptsubscriptрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptв„¬рқ‘ӣрқ‘Ұsuperscriptрқ‘ӣвҖІрқ‘ҡ1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle+\frac{1}{q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d)}\sum_{n^{\prime}\in\mathcal{N}_{n}^{k*}(d)\cap\mathcal{B}_{n}}y(n^{\prime},m)\frac{1}{N^{*}_{n}}вүӨ\displaystyle\leqqnвҲ’BnqnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҖӢ1NnвҲ—+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)qnвҲ’Bn+BnkвҒЈвҲ—вҖӢ(d)вҖӢ1NnвҲ—=1NnвҲ—.subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘subscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқҗөрқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқҗөрқ‘ҳрқ‘ӣрқ‘‘1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣ1subscriptsuperscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣ\displaystyle\frac{q_{n}-B_{n}}{q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d)}\frac{1}{N^{*}_{n}}+\frac{B^{k*}_{n}(d)}{q_{n}-B_{n}+B^{k*}_{n}(d)}\frac{1}{N^{*}_{n}}=\frac{1}{N^{*}_{n}}.

Verification of (c6). Note that Assumption 4 guarantees that any subgraph removing all agents in рқ’Ірқ’І\mathcal{W} and any additional qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} incoming edges at honest agent nрқ‘ӣn has a source node nвҲ—superscriptрқ‘ӣn^{*} and it can reach any other agent within П„рқ’ўsubscriptрқңҸрқ’ў\tau_{\mathcal{G}} steps. Therefore, no element in the nвҲ—superscriptрқ‘ӣn^{*}-th column of matrix (рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d))П„рқ’ўsuperscriptsuperscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқңҸрқ’ў(\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d))^{\tau_{\mathcal{G}}} is zero.

To show that there exist no more than Hрқ’ўsubscriptрқҗ»рқ’ўH_{\mathcal{G}} types of рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d), notice that each рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d) containing at least NnвҲ’qn+1subscriptрқ‘Ғрқ‘ӣsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣ1N_{n}-q_{n}+1 non-zero elements corresponds to a subgraph obtained by removing all Byzantine agents with their edges, and removing any additional qnsubscriptрқ‘һрқ‘ӣq_{n} incoming edges at honest node nрқ‘ӣn. Every such subgraph is contained in в„Ӣрқ’ўsubscriptв„Ӣрқ’ў\mathcal{H}_{\mathcal{G}}, whose cardinality is Hрқ’ўsubscriptрқҗ»рқ’ўH_{\mathcal{G}}.

Now all conditions have been verified, and thus Theorems 3 and 4 can be applied to Byrd-TD(О»рқңҶ\lambda).

the first inequality comes from the fact (x+y)2вүӨ2вҖӢx2+2вҖӢy2superscriptрқ‘Ҙрқ‘Ұ22superscriptрқ‘Ҙ22superscriptрқ‘Ұ2(x+y)^{2}\leq 2x^{2}+2y^{2}, рқҡҪcsubscriptрқҡҪрқ‘җ\mathbf{\Phi}_{c} is defined Combining with (18), (C.2) implies the following boundFвҖӢ(рқңҪnk+1)вүӨрқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣabsent\displaystyle F(\bm{\theta}^{k+1}_{n})\leqПғcвҖӢвҖ–рқңҪnk+1вҲ’рқңҪО»вҲһвҖ–2+2вҖӢFвҖӢ(рқңҪО»вҲһ)вүӨПғcвҖӢвҖ–рқңҪnk+1вҲ’рқңҪО»вҲһвҖ–2+2вҖӢ1вҲ’ОівҖӢО»1вҲ’ОівҖӢminрқңҪвҒЎFвҖӢ(рқңҪ).subscriptрқңҺрқ‘җsuperscriptnormsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ22рқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶsubscriptрқңҺрқ‘җsuperscriptnormsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ221рқӣҫрқңҶ1рқӣҫsubscriptрқңҪрқҗ№рқңҪ\displaystyle\sigma_{c}\|\bm{\theta}^{k+1}_{n}-\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}\|^{2}+2F(\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda})\leq\sigma_{c}\|\bm{\theta}^{k+1}_{n}-\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}\|^{2}+2\frac{1-\gamma\lambda}{1-\gamma}\min_{\bm{\theta}}F(\bm{\theta}).(97)

Plugging (23) into (97), summing up over nвҲҲрқ’©рқ‘ӣрқ’©n\in\mathcal{N} and taking limits on both sides of (97) yieldlimkвҶ’вҲһsup1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©FвҖӢ(рқңҪnk+1)subscriptвҶ’рқ‘ҳsupremum1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©рқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣ\displaystyle\lim_{k\to\infty}\sup\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}F(\bm{\theta}^{k+1}_{n})вүӨ\displaystyle\leqlimkвҶ’вҲһsup1NвҖӢвҲ‘nвҲҲрқ’©ПғcвҖӢвҖ–рқңҪnk+1вҲ’рқңҪО»вҲһвҖ–2+2вҖӢFвҖӢ(рқңҪО»вҲһ)subscriptвҶ’рқ‘ҳsupremum1рқ‘Ғsubscriptрқ‘ӣрқ’©subscriptрқңҺрқ‘җsuperscriptnormsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқ‘ҳ1рқ‘ӣsubscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ22рқҗ№subscriptsuperscriptрқңҪрқңҶ\displaystyle\lim_{k\to\infty}\sup\frac{1}{N}\sum_{n\in\mathcal{N}}\sigma_{c}\|\bm{\theta}^{k+1}_{n}-\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda}\|^{2}+2F(\bm{\theta}^{\infty}_{\lambda})вүӨ\displaystyle\leq2вҖӢC4вҖӢDрқ’ўвҖӢОҙ2(1вҲ’ОівҖӢО»)2+2вҖӢ1вҲ’ОівҖӢО»1вҲ’ОівҖӢminрқңҪвҒЎFвҖӢ(рқңҪ).2subscriptрқҗ¶4subscriptрқҗ·рқ’ўsuperscriptрқӣҝ2superscript1рқӣҫрқңҶ221рқӣҫрқңҶ1рқӣҫsubscriptрқңҪрқҗ№рқңҪ\displaystyle 2C_{4}\frac{D_{\mathcal{G}}\delta^{2}}{(1-\gamma\lambda)^{2}}+2\frac{1-\gamma\lambda}{1-\gamma}\min_{\bm{\theta}}F(\bm{\theta}).(98)This completes the proof.

Note that Condition (c6) guarantees that there exists at least one column of (рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d))П„рқ’ўsuperscriptsuperscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘subscriptрқңҸрқ’ў(\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d))^{\tau_{\mathcal{G}}}, denoted as the nвҲ—superscriptрқ‘ӣn^{*}-th column, being non-zero element-wise, and there exist no more than Hрқ’ўsubscriptрқҗ»рқ’ўH_{\mathcal{G}} choices of рқҗҳkвҖӢ(d)superscriptрқҗҳрқ‘ҳрқ‘‘\mathbf{Y}^{k}(d). Similar to (Vaidya, 2012, Lemma 3), for a row-stochastic matrix рқҗ–рқҗ–\mathbf{W}, we
